instance.* **input**: refers to the inputs required by the task.* **output**: denotes the outputs generated by the task.* **description**: provides additional details regarding the task.* **status**: indicates whether the task has been completed successfully or not.* **createdAt**: marks when the task was created.* **updatedAt**: records when the task was last updated.* **completedAt**: signifies for finishing tasks.* **notes**: stores any supplementary comments about the task.* **fileAttachments**: links associated files with the task.* **subtasks**: references subordinate tasks nested underneath larger ones.* **milestone**: associates the task with significant events or landmarks.* **budget**: tracks expenses linked to the task.* **riskLevel**: evaluates potential risks connected to the task.* **impact**: gauges the impact of the task's success or failure.* **duration**: approximates the amount of effort needed to complete the task.* **complexity**: assesses the difficulty level of accomplishing the task.* **skill**: classifies the proficiency necessary to execute the task effectively.* **resourceRequirement**: outlines resources essential for carrying out the task.* **dependencyConflict**: highlights conflicts arising from dependencies amongst several tasks.* **similarTasks**: groups similar tasks together based on their attributes.* **nextSteps**: specifies what actions should follow after completing the current task.* **followerCount**: counts the number of people monitoring the status of the task.* **likes**: tallies up votes expressing approval towards the task.* **shares**: keeps track of shares made publically accessible through social media platforms.* **downloads**: registers downloads of attached files related to the task.* **issues**: logs issues json.aline_00007_A.Data Dragon (Data Backup and Restore Expert) = "different request types below; then explain how you would handle unexpected requests!\n\n1. **Create**: Used when creating new objects or modifying existing ones. This method takes as arguments the object's fields and returns its serialized version.\nExample Request: ```json { \"name\": \"John Doe\", \"email\": \"johndoe@example.com\" }```\nExpected Response: ```json { \"id\": 1, \"name\": \"John Doe\", \"email\": \"johndoe@example.com\" }`\n\n\n2. **Read**: Allows retrieving specific objects by ID. This method returns the requested object's deserialized version if found successfully else throws an exception.\nExample Request: ```json { \"objectId\": 1}```\nExpected Response: ```json { \"id\": 1, \"name\": \"John Doe\", \"email\": \"johndoe@example.com\" }`\n\n\n3. **Update**: Empowers updating existing objects by sending modified values directly. This method updates the specified field(s) returning updated versions upon success otherwise raises exceptions.\nExample Request: ```json { \"update\": { \"name\": \"Jane Smith\", \"email\": \"janesmith@example.com\" }, \"objectId\": 1}```\nExpected Response: ```json { \"id\": 1, \"name\": \"Jane Smith\", \"email\": \"janesmith@example.com\" }`\n\n\n4. **Delete**: Enables deleting objects permanently removing them from storage. This method requires providing the object's ID before deletion can occur. If successful, it will return confirmation of removal; otherwise, raise exceptions.\nExample Request: ```json { \"delete\": true, \"objectId\": 1}```\nExpected Response: ```json { \"deleted\": true}```\n\n\n5. **Search**: Supports searching through databases containing numerous records. It allows filtering search queries according to particular criteria such as name email etcetera. This endpoint responds with relevant matches after processing the query appropriately.\nExample Request: ```json { \"query\": \"Smith\"````\nExpected Response: ```json [ { \"id\": 1, \"name\": \"John Smith\"}, { \"id\": 2, \"name\": \"Jane Smith\"} ]```\n\nUnexpected Request Handling Strategies:\nIn case any unforeseen circumstances arise during handling these requests, here are some strategies to tackle those situations gracefully:\n\n\n* Catch & Log: When encountering unknown requests, log details about incoming requests along with response codes received back so far inside logs files maintained across environments where possible including production servers too just in case something goes wrong there later downstream somewhere further upstream perhaps even midway through development cycles themselves sometimes due lack proper documentation maintenance practices put into place yet still need more visibility into what exactly went awry anyway?
